please tell us the details for this languages.

Reviewed 20 sources

Here is an overview of the programming languages listed in your screenshot. Each language is described with key features, uses, and characteristics.wikipedia+6

C++

C++ is a high-level, general-purpose programming language developed by Bjarne Stroustrup in 1985 as an extension of C. It supports both procedural and object-oriented programming and offers direct hardware access with efficient abstraction capabilities. C++ is widely used for developing system software, game engines, embedded systems, and high-performance applications. Its Standard Template Library (STL) provides a vast set of algorithms and data structures.geeksforgeeks+1

Java

Java is an object-oriented, platform-independent language created by Sun Microsystems. It's commonly used for web applications, mobile (Android), enterprise software, and server-side solutions due to its portabilitycode runs on any device with a Java Virtual Machine (JVM).wikipedia

Python (Python3 and Python)

Python is a high-level, interpreted language known for its simplicity and readability. It supports multiple programming paradigms, including procedural, object-oriented, and functional. Python is heavily used in web development, data science, automation, artificial intelligence, and academic research. Python3 is the latest major version, with improved syntax and features over Python2.wikipedia

JavaScript and TypeScript

JavaScript is the primary scripting language for web development, allowing interactive and dynamic content in browsers. TypeScript is a superset of JavaScript that includes static types, helping catch errors at compile time, and is popular for large, maintainable projects.wikipedia

C#

C# is a modern, object-oriented language developed by Microsoft. It is used mainly for developing Windows applications, backend servers (ASP.NET), and game development with Unity engine.wikipedia

C

C is a foundational, procedural programming language known for its speed and low-level memory management. Many operating systems and embedded systems are written in C, and it heavily influenced many other languages on this list.wikipedia

Go

Go, also known as Golang, was designed at Google in 2007 for system and network programming. It emphasizes simplicity, fast compilation, garbage collection, and excellent concurrency support via goroutines and channels. Go is popular for cloud services, servers, and scalable backend infrastructure.coursera+2

Kotlin

Kotlin is a statically typed language developed by JetBrains, officially supported for Android development. It combines functional and object-oriented features, and interoperates with Java code easily.wikipedia

Swift

Swift is Apples modern language for iOS, macOS, and watchOS app development. It offers safety features, fast performance, and expressive syntax.wikipedia

Rust

Rust is a system programming language focused on safety, performance, and concurrency. It prevents common bugs (like null pointer dereferencing and memory leaks), making it popular for systems, web assembly, and CLI tools.wikipedia

Ruby

Ruby is a dynamic, object-oriented language best known for web development with frameworks like Ruby on Rails. It emphasizes developer productivity and clean syntax.wikipedia

PHP

PHP is a popular scripting language for server-side web development, powering many websites and frameworks like WordPress.wikipedia

Dart

Dart is developed by Google, mainly used for front-end frameworks like Flutter to create cross-platform mobile apps. It focuses on performance and fast development cycles.wikipedia

Scala

Scala is a JVM language combining object-oriented and functional programming. Its used for big data tools (like Apache Spark) and scalable backend services.wikipedia

Elixir

Elixir is a functional, concurrent language running on the Erlang VM (BEAM). Its designed for scalable, fault-tolerant systems and is widely used in web applications and real-time distributed systems. Elixir leverages lightweight processes for highly concurrent applications.wikipedia+1

Erlang

Erlang is a concurrent language known for building robust, distributed, fault-tolerant systems. Its foundational in telecom and messaging platforms.elixir-lang+1

Racket

Racket is a descendant of the Lisp family of languages, focused on functional and academic use. Its used for scripting, computer science education, and language design research.wikipedia

If you need deeper details about any specific languagesyntax, applications, or ecosystemlet me know for a focused comparison or tutorial.wikipedia+6

procedures to learn these languages

Reviewed 20 sources

To learn the languages listed in your screenshot, here are the recommended step-by-step procedures for C++, Go, and Elixir. These processes are similar for other languagesbeginner-friendly, hands-on, and adaptable for self-study.codesignal+2

How to Learn C++

  • Set Up Environment

    • Install a C++ compiler (such as GCC, Clang, or MSVC) and an IDE (like Visual Studio Code, Code::Blocks, or Eclipse).codesignal

  • Start with Basics

    • Write a simple "Hello, World!" program to understand syntax and compiling/running code.codesignal

    • Learn about variables, data types, input/output, operators, and control structures (if, for, while loops).codesignal

  • Foundational Topics

    • Study functions, arrays, and pointers, then progress to object-oriented conceptsclasses, inheritance, and polymorphism.codesignal

  • Practice Regularly

    • Solve beginner exercises and build small projects like calculators or games.codesignal

  • Explore Advanced Concepts

    • Learn about templates, Standard Template Library (STL), memory management, and data structures.codesignal

  • Resources

    • Use tutorials (e.g., W3Schools, LearnCpp.com, GeeksforGeeks) and books for depth.codesignal

How to Learn Go (Golang)

  • Install Go

    • Download Go from the official website and set up your environment variables; install a code editor with Go extensions (such as VS Code).freecodecamp

  • Run Your First Code

    • Write a "Hello, World!" CLI tool or a simple web server using Gos built-in packages.freecodecamp

  • Understand Syntax

    • Learn Go basics: data types, variables, operators, functions, methods, and packages.freecodecamp

  • Project-Based Practice

    • Build practical projects such as backend services or REST APIs using frameworks like Gin.freecodecamp

    • Explore concurrency in Go with goroutines and channels.freecodecamp

  • Documentation and Community

    • Study official Go guides, online courses, and open-source projects for reference.freecodecamp

How to Learn Elixir

  • Set Up Environment

    • Install Elixir and set up an editor (VS Code or another that supports Elixir).codesignal

  • Foundational Concepts

    • Study variables, data types, and the basics of functional programmingfunctions, modules, pattern matching, and recursion.codesignal

  • Hands-On Practice

    • Solve exercises focusing on functional programming and concurrency.codesignal

  • Learn OTP/Erlang VM

    • Dive deeper into the Erlang VM and OTP for building concurrent, distributed applications.codesignal

  • Projects and Further Learning

    • Build sample Elixir applications to practice what you learn, leveraging online courses, video tutorials, and interactive learning platforms.codesignal

  • Recommended Resources

    • Consult guides like Elixir School, CodeSignal, and the official site for step-by-step courses.codesignal

General Steps for Learning Any Language

  • Set up the languages runtime and editor or IDE.

  • Learn the syntax and basic programming concepts.

  • Build and debug simple projects (e.g., calculators, web servers).

  • Practice regularly with exercises and coding challenges.

  • Read documentation and join developer communities.

If you want procedures for other languages on your list (Java, Python, JavaScript, etc.), mention a language for specific steps.freecodecamp+2

learning in a way to learn all languages

1 step completed

To learn all the programming languages shown in your screenshot efficiently, use a universal, structured approach focused on problem-solving and concept mastery. This helps you transfer learning across languages and accelerates your growth as a multilingual programmer.codesignal+2

Universal Method to Learn Programming Languages

1. Set Up the Environment

  • Install the compiler/interpreter and a code editor or IDE for each language you study.freecodecamp+1

  • Configure your system for rapid developmentusing extensions or plugins for code completion, linting, and debugging.codesignal

2. Master the Fundamentals

  • For each language, start with basic syntax, variables, data types, input/output, and operators.codesignal+2

  • Focus on control structures: if/else, loops, and error handling.codesignal

  • Write Hello, World! and simple arithmetic programs in every language.freecodecamp+1

3. Practice Common Patterns

  • Implement universal programming patternsfunctions, recursion, data structures (arrays, lists, stacks, queues), and file I/O.freecodecamp+1

  • Build the same small projects (calculator, to-do app, simple game) in multiple languages to compare syntax and logic.codesignal

4. Learn Advanced Concepts Gradually

  • Study object-oriented programming, functional programming, and concurrency as each language supports them.codesignal+1

  • Explore each languages specific features (e.g., modules in Python, classes in C++, goroutines in Go, pattern matching in Elixir).codesignal+1

5. Solve Real Problems

  • Practice coding challenges on platforms like LeetCode, HackerRank, CodeSignal using all languages you know.freecodecamp+1

  • Try porting solutions between languages for deeper understanding.codesignal

6. Read Documentation and Explore Learning Platforms

  • Use official documentation and community tutorials for language-specific guidance.codesignal+2

  • Participate in discussion boards or local study groups for help and peer learning.codesignal

Tips for Learning Multiple Languages Efficiently

  • Group languages by paradigmobject-oriented (Java, C++, C#), functional (Elixir, Scala, Racket), scripting/web (JavaScript, PHP, Python)and learn core concepts together.freecodecamp+1

  • Alternate between languages weekly or combine their learning through universal projects.

  • Build conceptual maps or comparison tables for syntax and common constructs.

  • Regularly reflect on similarities and differences to reinforce transferable knowledge.

Apply this structured method to each language in your listprogressing from basics, practicing consistently, and using online resources for support. This approach ensures comprehensive, comparative, and practical learning across all major programming languages.codesignal+2

I am asking that which language is learning first then second then third to complete all the programming language listed in the screenshot

1 step completed

For best results, begin learning programming languages in an order that builds foundational skills and makes it easier to transition to more complex or specialized languages. Heres a recommended learning sequence based on your screenshot, starting from fundamental, industry-standard languages and progressing to advanced, niche, or modern languages.codesignal+1

Recommended Order to Learn the Listed Languages

  1. C
    Start here for core programming concepts, memory management, and procedural programming. It provides a strong foundation for understanding how computers work.codesignal

  2. C++
    Builds on C, introduces object-oriented programming and advanced features. Valuable for competitive coding and performance-critical development.codesignal

  3. Python / Python3
    Easy to learn, widely used in automation, web, data science, and scripting. Python3 is recommended as its the latest version.freecodecamp+1

  4. Java
    Introduces robust, cross-platform object-oriented programming. Used in Android, web, and enterprise software development.codesignal

  5. JavaScript
    Essential for web development, interactive front-end coding. Useful after mastering basic programming concepts.freecodecamp

  6. TypeScript
    Builds on JavaScript, adds powerful typing, better suited for large-scale web projects after learning JavaScript.freecodecamp

  7. C#
    Microsofts main language for desktop, gaming, and enterprise apps via .NET and Unity.codesignal

  8. Go (Golang)
    Modern language for scalable, concurrent backend/server work. Recommended after grasping basics of object-oriented and procedural languages.freecodecamp

  9. Kotlin
    Valuable for Android/mobile development. Pair with Java knowledge for best results.codesignal

  10. Swift
    Used for iOS/Mac development. Learn after mastering object-oriented paradigms.codesignal

  11. PHP
    Popular for server-side scripting and web backends. Learn after JavaScript for practical web development skills.codesignal

  12. Ruby
    Scripting and web (Rails framework). Easy, expressive syntax; best after Python and JavaScript experience.codesignal

  13. Rust
    Focused on safety and performance. Learn after C/C++ for advanced systems programming knowledge.freecodecamp

  14. Dart
    Main language for Flutter (cross-platform apps). Good after grasping JavaScript and mobile development basics.freecodecamp

  15. Scala
    Combines object-oriented and functional programming. Useful after Java; often used in distributed computing and big data.codesignal

  16. Elixir
    Functional, concurrent programming for scalable systems. Beneficial after understanding functional concepts (from Python, JavaScript, Scala).codesignal

  17. Erlang
    Excellent for concurrency and distributed systems. Learn alongside or after Elixir as theyre closely related.codesignal

  18. Racket
    Functional, academic, and scripting use. Suitable for deepening understanding of language design and functional programming paradigms.codesignal

How to Approach the Sequence

  • Start with C or Python for simple syntax and strong computational thinking.

  • Build up to object-oriented and web languages (C++, Java, JavaScript).

  • Add modern or specialized languages (Go, Kotlin, Swift, etc.) after foundational skills.

  • Explore functional and concurrent languages (Scala, Elixir, Erlang, Racket) at the end, as they require deeper conceptual insight.

Following this progression will make it easier to learn each subsequent language quickly, as many concepts are transferable.codesignal+2
